	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Greco-Persian Wars</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
		<div id="contentSub"><span class="mw-redirectedfrom">&#160;&#160;(Redirected from <a href="/w/index.php?title=Persian_Wars&amp;redirect=no" class="mw-redirect" title="Persian Wars">Persian Wars</a>)</span></div>
		
		
		
		<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>
		<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">"Persian Wars" redirects here. For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/Persian_Wars_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Persian Wars (disambiguation)">Persian Wars (disambiguation)</a>.</div>
<div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">series of conflicts between the Achaemenid Empire of Persia and poleis of the Hellenic world in the fifth century BC</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>

<div role="navigation" class="navbox" aria-labelledby="Greco-Persian_Wars" style="margin:0;float:right;clear:right;width:25.5em;margin-bottom:0.5em;margin-left:1em;;padding:3px"><table class="nowraplinks navbox-vertical mw-collapsible autocollapse navbox-inner" style="border-spacing:0;background:transparent;color:inherit"><tbody><tr><th scope="col" class="navbox-title" colspan="2" style="background-color:#C3D6EF;"><div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Campaignbox_Greco-Persian_Wars" title="Template:Campaignbox Greco-Persian Wars"><abbr title="View this template" style=";background-color:#C3D6EF;;background:none transparent;border:none;-moz-box-shadow:none;-webkit-box-shadow:none;box-shadow:none; padding:0;">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Campaignbox_Greco-Persian_Wars" title="Template talk:Campaignbox Greco-Persian Wars"><abbr title="Discuss this template" style=";background-color:#C3D6EF;;background:none transparent;border:none;-moz-box-shadow:none;-webkit-box-shadow:none;box-shadow:none; padding:0;">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Campaignbox_Greco-Persian_Wars&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template" style=";background-color:#C3D6EF;;background:none transparent;border:none;-moz-box-shadow:none;-webkit-box-shadow:none;box-shadow:none; padding:0;">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div><div id="Greco-Persian_Wars" style="font-size:114%;margin:0 4em"><span style="line-height:1.6em"><a class="mw-selflink selflink"><span class="wrap">Greco-Persian Wars</span></a></span></div></th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" class="navbox-list navbox-odd hlist" style="width:100%;padding:0px"><div style="padding:0em 0.25em">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Ionian_Revolt" title="Ionian Revolt">Ionian Revolt</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/First_Persian_invasion_of_Greece" title="First Persian invasion of Greece">First Persian invasion</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Second_Persian_invasion_of_Greece" title="Second Persian invasion of Greece">Second Persian invasion</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Greco-Persian_Wars#Greek_counterattack_(479–478_BC)" title="Greco-Persian Wars">Greek counterattack</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Wars_of_the_Delian_League" title="Wars of the Delian League">Wars of the Delian League</a></li></ul>
</div></td></tr></tbody></table></div>
<p>The <b>Greco-Persian Wars</b> (also often called the <b>Persian Wars</b>) were a series of conflicts between the  <a href="/wiki/Achaemenid_Empire" title="Achaemenid Empire">Achaemenid Empire</a> and <a href="/wiki/Polis" title="Polis">Greek city-states</a> that started in 499 BC<sup id="ref_i" class="reference"><a href="#cnote_i">&#91;i&#93;</a></sup> and lasted until 449 BC. The collision between the fractious political world of the Greeks and the enormous empire of the Persians began when <a href="/wiki/Cyrus_the_Great" title="Cyrus the Great">Cyrus the Great</a> conquered the Greek-inhabited region of <a href="/wiki/Ionia" title="Ionia">Ionia</a> in 547 BC. Struggling to control the independent-minded cities of Ionia, the Persians appointed <a href="/wiki/Tyrant#Historical_forms" title="Tyrant">tyrants</a> to rule each of them. This would prove to be the source of much trouble for the Greeks and Persians alike.
</p><p>In 499 BC, the tyrant of <a href="/wiki/Miletus" title="Miletus">Miletus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aristagoras" title="Aristagoras">Aristagoras</a>, embarked on an <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Naxos_(499_BC)" title="Siege of Naxos (499 BC)">expedition</a> to conquer the island of <a href="/wiki/Naxos_Island" class="mw-redirect" title="Naxos Island">Naxos</a>, with Persian support;<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> however, the expedition was a debacle and, preempting his dismissal, Aristagoras incited all of Hellenic <a href="/wiki/Asia_Minor" class="mw-redirect" title="Asia Minor">Asia Minor</a> into rebellion against the Persians. This was the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/Ionian_Revolt" title="Ionian Revolt">Ionian Revolt</a>, which would last until 493 BC, progressively drawing more regions of Asia Minor into the conflict. Aristagoras secured military support from <a href="/wiki/Classical_Athens" title="Classical Athens">Athens</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eretria" title="Eretria">Eretria</a>, and in 498 BC these forces helped to capture and burn the Persian regional capital of <a href="/wiki/Sardis" title="Sardis">Sardis</a>. The Persian king <a href="/wiki/Darius_the_Great" title="Darius the Great">Darius the Great</a> vowed to have revenge on Athens and Eretria for this act. The revolt continued, with the two sides effectively stalemated throughout 497–495 BC. In 494 BC, the Persians regrouped and attacked the epicenter of the revolt in Miletus. At the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Lade" title="Battle of Lade">Battle of Lade</a>, the Ionians suffered a decisive defeat, and the rebellion collapsed, with the final members being stamped out the following year.
</p><p>Seeking to secure his empire from further revolts and from the interference of the mainland Greeks, Darius embarked on a scheme to conquer Greece and to punish Athens and Eretria for the burning of Sardis. The <a href="/wiki/First_Persian_invasion_of_Greece" title="First Persian invasion of Greece">first Persian invasion of Greece</a> began in 492 BC, with the Persian general <a href="/wiki/Mardonius_(general)" title="Mardonius (general)">Mardonius</a> successfully re-subjugating <a href="/wiki/Thrace" title="Thrace">Thrace</a> and <a href="/wiki/Macedon" class="mw-redirect" title="Macedon">Macedon</a> before several mishaps forced an early end to the rest of the campaign.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERoismanWorthington2011135-138_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERoismanWorthington2011135-138-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> In 490 BC a second force was sent to Greece, this time across the <a href="/wiki/Aegean_Sea" title="Aegean Sea">Aegean Sea</a>, under the command of <a href="/wiki/Datis" title="Datis">Datis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Artaphernes_(son_of_Artaphernes)" title="Artaphernes (son of Artaphernes)">Artaphernes</a>. This expedition subjugated the <a href="/wiki/Cyclades" title="Cyclades">Cyclades</a>, before <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Eretria" title="Siege of Eretria">besieging, capturing and razing Eretria</a>. However, while en route to attack Athens, the Persian force was decisively defeated by the Athenians at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Marathon" title="Battle of Marathon">Battle of Marathon</a>, ending Persian efforts for the time being.
</p><p>Darius then began to plan to completely conquer Greece but died in 486 BC and responsibility for the conquest passed to his son <a href="/wiki/Xerxes_I" title="Xerxes I">Xerxes</a>. In 480 BC, Xerxes personally led the <a href="/wiki/Second_Persian_invasion_of_Greece" title="Second Persian invasion of Greece">second Persian invasion of Greece</a> with one of the largest ancient armies ever assembled. Victory over the allied Greek states at the famous <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Thermopylae" title="Battle of Thermopylae">Battle of Thermopylae</a> allowed the Persians to torch an evacuated Athens and overrun most of Greece. However, while seeking to destroy the combined Greek fleet, the Persians suffered a severe defeat at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Salamis" title="Battle of Salamis">Battle of Salamis</a>. The following year, the confederated Greeks went on the offensive, decisively defeating the Persian army at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Plataea" title="Battle of Plataea">Battle of Plataea</a>, and ending the invasion of Greece by the Achaemenid Empire.
</p><p>The allied Greeks followed up their success by destroying the rest of the Persian fleet at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Mycale" title="Battle of Mycale">Battle of Mycale</a>, before expelling Persian garrisons from <a href="/wiki/Sestos" title="Sestos">Sestos</a> (479 BC) and <a href="/wiki/Byzantium" title="Byzantium">Byzantium</a> (478 BC). Following the Persian withdrawal from Europe and the Greek victory at Mycale, Macedon and the city-states of Ionia regained their independence. The actions of the general <a href="/wiki/Pausanias_(general)" title="Pausanias (general)">Pausanias</a> at the siege of Byzantium alienated many of the Greek states from the Spartans, and the anti-Persian alliance was therefore reconstituted around Athenian leadership, called the <a href="/wiki/Delian_League" title="Delian League">Delian League</a>. The Delian League <a href="/wiki/Wars_of_the_Delian_League" title="Wars of the Delian League">continued to campaign</a> against Persia for the next three decades, beginning with the expulsion of the remaining Persian garrisons from <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>. At the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Eurymedon" title="Battle of the Eurymedon">Battle of the Eurymedon</a> in 466 BC, the League won a double victory that finally secured freedom for the cities of Ionia. However, the League's involvement in the <a href="/wiki/Artaxerxes_I_of_Persia#Egyptian_revolt" title="Artaxerxes I of Persia">Egyptian revolt</a> by <a href="/wiki/Inaros_II" title="Inaros II">Inaros II</a> against <a href="/wiki/Artaxerxes_I" class="mw-redirect" title="Artaxerxes I">Artaxerxes I</a> (from 460–454 BC) resulted in a disastrous defeat, and further campaigning was suspended. A Greek fleet was sent to <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Cyprus</a> in 451 BC, but achieved little, and, when it withdrew, the Greco-Persian Wars drew to a quiet end. Some historical sources suggest the end of hostilities was marked by a peace treaty between Athens and Persia, the <a href="/wiki/Peace_of_Callias" title="Peace of Callias">Peace of Callias</a>.
</p>
